<div id="review_1657997927" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1657997927" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1657997927?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=distant-lands">distant-lands</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=free-from-work">free-from-work</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1657997927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17955685837673179830"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best fantasy AND debut goodreads author! what will happen?</b><br/><br/>this is a stunning debut that perfectly mimics the tone of a classic fairytale, but breathes new and exciting life into the familiar themes with lyrical writing, strong characters, and by weaving in elements of russian folklore, which were mostly unfamiliar to me, and therefore fresh and exotic.<br/><br/>quickplot first, then i will return to these three strengths in greater detail.<br/><br/>pyotr vladimirovich </span>
  <span id="freeText17955685837673179830" style="display:none"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best fantasy AND debut goodreads author! what will happen?</b><br><br>this is a stunning debut that perfectly mimics the tone of a classic fairytale, but breathes new and exciting life into the familiar themes with lyrical writing, strong characters, and by weaving in elements of russian folklore, which were mostly unfamiliar to me, and therefore fresh and exotic.<br><br>quickplot first, then i will return to these three strengths in greater detail.<br><br>pyotr vladimirovich is a lord in medieval rus', responsible for the well-being of several villages in the heavily-forested wilderness, subject to his late wife marina's half-brother, the grand prince in moscow. he has five children, the youngest of which is a daughter named vasilisa/vasya, whose birth caused marina's death. it was a risky, late pregnancy, but marina was determined to have her, knowing that vasya would be her only child gifted with the magical birthright held by her bloodline's women. vasya grows up with a curious mind and a wandering nature - dressing like a boy, drawn to exploring the forest, and befriending the house spirits the villagers all leave ritual offerings for, in a long-standing superstitious tradition, but which only she is able to see. it's a hard life, with food shortages during the long cold winters, and vasya's latent power attracts the attention of morozko, an old spirit personifying the relentless cold known by many different appellations: demon of winter, death-god, frost demon, winter-king. when pyotr is in moscow arranging his daughter olga's marriage, and unexpectedly finding himself married off to an equally-reluctant bride as a political favor, morozko is insulted by one of pyotr's sons, whom he allows to live in exchange for the promise of vasya's hand in marriage. this arrangement dismays vasya's nurse dunya, who tries to put it off as long as possible, and it is more or less forgotten as time passes and more pressing concerns arise, specifically the influence of an ambitious priest, adored by vasya's stepmother, who forbids the villagers to continue their practice of acknowledging the household spirits, which results in horrors only vasya has the power to prevent. <br><br>arden's writing is the book's strongest selling point: evocative, beautifully descriptive, imagery that pops with details alive enough to make you smell the smoke and feel the cold; it's haunting, vivid, and poetic. when pyotr and his sons leave their village in order to meet with their royal relative in moscow, they encounter <i>a city of smiling enemies and barbed favors</i> described as <i>lusty and squalid, like a fair woman with feet caked in filth.</i> <br><br>occasionally, it can get a little <i>too</i> adjective-crazed:<br><br><i>Great trees threw sooty shadows onto the raw wood of the little church.</i><br><br>but for the most part, it is well-controlled .<br><br>character is also an easy sell - vasilisa, like all of the best fairytale heroines, is the inheritor of a great responsibility; the fulfillment of a prophecy that is equal parts burden and gift. her wildness is part of her appeal; power and freedom and all the beauty and mystery of nature: <i>She looked like a wild thing new-caught and just barely groomed into submission.</i> she doesn't know the extent of her powers, or even that she <i>has</i> powers, but they can be felt by others, like her father, who understands that the ordinary roles available to women; wife and mother, would ruin something essential to her character.<br><br><i>"She is a handsome girl," said Pyotr. "Though a savage. She needs a husband; it would steady her." But as he spoke, an image came to him of his wild girl wedded and bedded, sweating over an oven. The image filled him with a strange regret, and he shook it away.</i><br><br>even the priest konstantin is drawn to her, despite his severity towards her, and laments the future he is nonetheless pushing her towards:<br><br><i>He saw all at once, as Pyotr had seen, the wild thing brought indoors, busy and breathless, a woman like other women. Like Pyotr, he felt a strange sorrow and shook it away. ..he thought again of years, of childbearing and exhaustion. The wildness gone, the hawk's grace chained up…He swallowed. It is for the best. The wildness was sinful.</i><br><br>for me, the themes were equally fascinating - i'm always drawn to books focused on transitional periods; clashes between tradition and modernity, the old ways and the new. one of the best of these is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/883995.Morality_Play" title="Morality Play by Barry Unsworth" rel="nofollow noopener">Morality Play</a> by barry unsworth, which is about a troupe of actors in the 1300's who dared perform a play that wasn't based upon biblical events and the uneasiness and backlash this causes. while christianity was by no means new to medieval rus', the confrontation here between religion and tradition is devastating, made more so by the fact that the offerings to the house spirits, followed by the villagers as a tradition with no real belief behind them, turn out to be all that is holding the evil at bay.<br><br>a beautiful debut, and i'm very excited to see what else she's got in the works.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17955685837673179830" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7612546221072691769">Magical is the word that best describes this unusual tale, in every sense. I have to say that I've not read anything quite like this one, but believe me, that IS meant as a compliment.<br/><br/>It transports the reader back to medieval Russia, to a place thick with forests and deep crisp glistening snow. It is here that we find Vasya, and her family. Vasya is a child of nature, a wild and wilful girl. She has powers that leave the villagers questioning the nature of those powers, many believing that she's</span>
  <span id="freeText7612546221072691769" style="display:none">Magical is the word that best describes this unusual tale, in every sense. I have to say that I've not read anything quite like this one, but believe me, that IS meant as a compliment.<br /><br />It transports the reader back to medieval Russia, to a place thick with forests and deep crisp glistening snow. It is here that we find Vasya, and her family. Vasya is a child of nature, a wild and wilful girl. She has powers that leave the villagers questioning the nature of those powers, many believing that she's a witch. It's difficult to go into too much detail without spoiling it for other readers, but this is a most unusual tale that reads like a fairytale but was written with a more adult audience in mind.<br /><br />The imagery is simply wonderful, the characters leap out of the page, and the storyline is a mixture of history and Russian folklore. What an ambitious debut novel this is, but Katherine Arden has pulled it off beautifully.<br /><br />*Thank you to Netgalley, Random House/Ebury, &amp; Katherine Arden for my ARC in exchange for a fair and honest</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2778628918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9575095816291242603"><i>
  <b>“Fairy tales are sweet on winter nights, nothing more.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>Every moment I spent reading <i>The Bear and the Nightingale</i> was an absolute pleasure. It was magical, atmospheric and very slow paced - so prepare yourself for that if you're going to be picking this up. <br/><br/>The writing was enchanting and I felt transported through words into this story. <br/><br/>Though this book is mainly about Vasya there are many chapters in POV of other characters and we get to know them as well. Arden gave us complex characters wh</span>
  <span id="freeText9575095816291242603" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“Fairy tales are sweet on winter nights, nothing more.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Every moment I spent reading <i>The Bear and the Nightingale</i> was an absolute pleasure. It was magical, atmospheric and very slow paced - so prepare yourself for that if you're going to be picking this up. <br /><br />The writing was enchanting and I felt transported through words into this story. <br /><br />Though this book is mainly about Vasya there are many chapters in POV of other characters and we get to know them as well. Arden gave us complex characters who are not all good. Most were selfish, power hungry and filled with fear. <br /><br />Vasya was such a joy to read about. I loved her wild nature and refusal to conform to her towns expectations. She was always authentically <i>Vasya</i> and I cannot wait to see her character growth in the sequels. <br /><br />Other characters I loved were Vasya's brother Alyosha and her nursemaid Dunya. I found Sasha's character really interesting and I hope we see him again in the future. <br /><br />The pacing does pick up towards the end. There were a plenty of scenes that had me teary eyed. There is still so much unexplored and characters (as I've mentioned) that I really am excited to get to see again. <br /><br /><b>Note: this is not YA, this series is adult fantasy. Thanks for coming to my Tedtalk</b><br /><br />__<br /><i>Pre-Read</i><br />It's the middle of winter where I am and that means <b>it is finally time</b> for me to read the Winternight Trilogy!! <br /><br />Coffee ✔ Cozy blanket ️✔️ Cats ✔️ Cold weather ✔️— I'M READY<br /><br />Like seriously guys I bought this series in December and I've been waiting months for the perfect winter conditions</span>
  <a data-text-id="9575095816291242603" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2211499921" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2211499921" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2211499921?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cristina Monica by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/14811808-liz">Liz</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2211499921" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9054184140465523973">This is the perfect book to read during wintertime, when there is snow falling from the sky and everything feels like magic.<br/><br/>Because this is such a magical and atmospheric book. I am glad the sequel just came out, since I could not see myself reading it under different weather conditions. <br/><br/>I knew close to nothing about Russian culture and folklore, so this was my introduction to the latter. Actually, I had heard of Ivan and Baba Yaga – but that is all and I was ashamed of myself, therefore I am ha</span>
  <span id="freeText9054184140465523973" style="display:none">This is the perfect book to read during wintertime, when there is snow falling from the sky and everything feels like magic.<br /><br />Because this is such a magical and atmospheric book. I am glad the sequel just came out, since I could not see myself reading it under different weather conditions. <br /><br />I knew close to nothing about Russian culture and folklore, so this was my introduction to the latter. Actually, I had heard of Ivan and Baba Yaga – but that is all and I was ashamed of myself, therefore I am happy I was able to learn some things from this book.<br /><br />You’d think that after having read more than a thousand books I wouldn’t still be this impressed and in awe when encountering beautifully-lyrical writings styles with vivid imagery in my reads. But I am, and the truth is, it’s not easy to write the way Katherine Arden does. She will fill your mind with wonder and feed your imagination. <br /><br />This is not a book you will read in one single sitting or even in one single day. It’s slow-paced and contains very little action as well as a limited amount of settings, but that’s okay. I did not mind, seeing that I can fall as hard for stories that are character-driven as the other sorts. In fact, I love that we see Vasya grow up into a strong, adventurous and courageous young woman. <br /><br />I would easily have given it a five-star rating had it not been so heavy on religion, but I understand that religion was and still is important to Russian culture. Furthermore, without the religious theme, this story would have been much shorter and less developed. On the other hand, throughout the story, I wished for Father Konstantin to make his disappearance once and for all, because he was trouble. <br /><br />Thank you, Katherine Arden, for writing this book. It is a diamond among semi precious stones. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>

<div id="review_1839087036" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1839087036" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1839087036?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/31344916-the-bear-and-the-nightingale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=east-europe-russia">east-europe-russia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1839087036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2432515570825077354">4.5 stars! Review first posted on <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>:<br/><br/>In the northern lands of medieval Rus’, a daughter is born to Pyotr Vladimirovich, a boyar, lord over many lands, and his wife Marina, who dies in childbirth. But Marina, daughter of the Grand Prince of Moscow and a mysterious, swan-like beggar girl, has bequeathed her daughter Vasilisa a mystical heritage.<br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484194601i/21692183._SY540_.jpg' width='240' height='375' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Vasilisa the Brave (or Beautiful)<br/><br/> Vasilisa, or Vasya, grows up to be a spirited and rather rebellious young girl who, like an untamed colt</span>
  <span id="freeText2432515570825077354" style="display:none">4.5 stars! Review first posted on <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>:<br><br>In the northern lands of medieval Rus’, a daughter is born to Pyotr Vladimirovich, a boyar, lord over many lands, and his wife Marina, who dies in childbirth. But Marina, daughter of the Grand Prince of Moscow and a mysterious, swan-like beggar girl, has bequeathed her daughter Vasilisa a mystical heritage.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484194601i/21692183._SY540_.jpg" width="240" height="375" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Vasilisa the Brave (or Beautiful)<br><br> Vasilisa, or Vasya, grows up to be a spirited and rather rebellious young girl who, like an untamed colt, freely roams the fields and forest, and is able to see and communicate with the domovoi (a guardian of the home), rusalka (a dangerous water nymph), and other natural spirits of the home and land. Her beloved nurse Dunya tells Vasya and her siblings stories of Ivan and the Gray Wolf, the Firebird, and the frost-king, Morozko.<br><br>But Vasya’s carefree life ends when her father finally decides to remarry. He brings home a new wife from Moscow, Anna, the daughter of the prince of Moscow, who is also able to see the spirits of the land, but considers them devils and demons, clinging to her cross and her belief in the church. Pyotr also brings home a mysterious gift for Vasya, a necklace with a brilliant silver-blue jewel, given to him by Morozko, whom he met in Moscow. But Pyotr and the old nurse Dunya hold the necklace back from Vasya, fearing to give it to her.<br><br>Vasya’s life with Anna as her stepmother becomes strained: the strictly devout Anna is always at odds with the child of nature, who loves the magical creatures that terrify Anna. Life becomes even more difficult when a new priest arrives from Moscow, Father Konstantin, a handsome and charismatic man who preaches fiery sermons against the spirits of the land. As the people cease honoring (and leaving food for) these spirits, they weaken … but evil is waiting to step in as their protective influence wanes. Vasya finds herself at odds with her family and the villagers as she strives to protect them against unimaginable dangers that they thought existed only in fairy tales.<br><br><i>The Bear and the Nightingale</i> weaves a richly colored tapestry, combining elements from various Russian fairy tales, a realistic description of life in medieval times, when Russia was not yet a unified country, and an independent an appealing heroine. The frost-king Morozko and his destructive brother, the Bear, play the primary fairy tale roles, but there are additional and sometimes delightfully unexpected Russian folklore elements like the stepmother sending her stepdaughter into the forest to find snowdrops in midwinter (from the story <a href="http://www.russfolkart.com/folkTales.htm#Twelve" rel="nofollow noopener">“Twelve Months”</a>), <a href="http://www.russfolkart.com/folkTales.htm#Morozko" rel="nofollow noopener">Morozko</a> (also known as Father Frost) sending lost girls home with a dowry of gold and jewels, the <a href="http://www.aaronshep.com/stories/032.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Sea-King’s daughter</a>, and <a href="http://www.russfolkart.com/folkTales.htm#Frog" rel="nofollow noopener">Vasilisa the Beautiful</a>. (I’m sure I missed a few more!)<br><br>The atmosphere is well-developed, immersing you in life in medieval Rus’, a place where fairy tales may be true … which is not necessarily a comfortable thing. Enchantments can be good or evil, and the rusalka, vazila (a spirit that guards the stable and livestock) and other nature spirits are dangerous as well as helpful. Arden deftly illustrates their nature, so alien to humankind, as well as the need for mutual understanding and cooperative co-existence, which breaks down so badly in this tale.<br><br>A major theme ― in fact, it propels the entire plot ― is the conflict between old beliefs, respecting and caring for the nature spirits, and the newer religion, Christianity, which is generally, and emphatically, in the wrong in this book. Father Konstantin and Anna, and the rest of the villagers that flock to follow the priest, are poor examples of religious believers. At times it seems that the novel sets up believers as being generally weak and dangerously misguided, if not evil, though those characters are offset, to some extent at least, by Vasya’s brother Sasha, who has a sincere heart and desire for a religious vocation, and the monk he follows, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergius_of_Radonezh" rel="nofollow noopener">Sergei Radonezhsky</a>. In any case, <i>The Bear and the Nightingale</i> certainly effectively illustrates the power of fear, as well as the danger of using that fear, rather than love, to prompt religious devotion.<br><br>Another prominent theme is Vasya’s desire to live life freely, on her own terms, in a time when an arranged marriage or life in a convent were generally the only options for a properly raised female. Though it’s a modern theme, Arden integrates it well into the overall plot, and Vasya doesn’t come off as unduly anachronistic … though I did get a little tired of seeing her compared to an unbroken filly.<br><br>The cruelty of winter and the terrors of the deep, untamed forest, where wolves ― and worse things ― rove, are tangible. At the same time, <i>The Bear and the Nightingale</i> also incorporates references to actual historic figures, like Genghis Khan (at this time the Rus’ people were required to pay tributes to the conquering Horde), Sergei Radonezhsky, and princes of Moscow from the fourteenth century, although they are fictionalized.<br><br><i>The Bear and the Nightingale</i> is a well-written and thoroughly thought-out fantasy, suspenseful and delightful. While it reads well as a stand-alone novel, Arden has indicated that two sequels are in process. I can’t wait to be transported to medieval Russia again!<br><br><b>Initial take:</b> This Russia-based fantasy, set in old times when it was not yet a unified country, mingles Russian fairy tales of nature spirits, the Frost King and his destructive brother, the Bear, and a young woman's desire to live life on her own terms when an arranged marriage or life in a convent seem to be the only options for her. When a charismatic young priest comes to their town and rails against the people's beliefs in the nature spirits, Vasya is one of the very few to resist him. And the priest's actions are leading to the weakening of the protective spirits and the strengthening of the Bear.<br><br>I wasn't entirely on board with the conflict between old beliefs and nature spirits and Christianity, which was generally in the wrong in this book. But other than that, it's very well-written and well thought out, with Russian fairy tales woven in in some unexpectedly delightful ways.<br><br><i>I received a free copy of this book from the publisher through NetGalley. Thank you!</i><br><br>Art credit: Photographer/artist is Viona Ielegems</span>
  <a data-text-id="2432515570825077354" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1858384124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1858384124" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1858384124?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1858384124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2353814010479561998"><b>An eerie, whimsical winter fairytale.</b><br/><blockquote>
  <i>❝ There was a time, not long ago<br/>When flowers grew all year<br/>When days were long<br/>And nights star-strewn<br/>And men lived free from fear ❞</i>
</blockquote><br/>Once upon a time, on the fringes of Russian wilderness, in a land of harsh winters wavering between superstition and the observance of the old spirits and demons and Christianity, a peculiar girl was born. She was untamed, <i>fey</i>, a cacophony. She could see and converse with sprites, she talked to horses, spent her days in the fore</span>
  <span id="freeText2353814010479561998" style="display:none"><b>An eerie, whimsical winter fairytale.</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>❝ There was a time, not long ago<br />When flowers grew all year<br />When days were long<br />And nights star-strewn<br />And men lived free from fear ❞</i>
</blockquote><br />Once upon a time, on the fringes of Russian wilderness, in a land of harsh winters wavering between superstition and the observance of the old spirits and demons and Christianity, a peculiar girl was born. She was untamed, <i>fey</i>, a cacophony. She could see and converse with sprites, she talked to horses, spent her days in the forest, and she was content until a fiery, gold-haired priest determined to instill the fear of God arrived in The Land of The Forest. As the offerings to the old ones were reduced, and fear gnawed at people's hearts, <b>an ancient evil force was slowly awakening in the woods</b>. A force beckoning to Vasya, calling for her blood. <i>The blood of the witch.</i> Is Vasya alone strong enough to defeat it, while her family turns against her, and her people blame her for their misfortunes? When famine strikes and the dead awaken, she will find the answer.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>❝ But seasons turn<br />The wind blows from the south<br />The fires come, the storms, the spears<br />The sorrow and the dark ❞</i>
</blockquote><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25489134.The_Bear_and_the_Nightingale__Winternight_Trilogy___1_" title="The Bear and the Nightingale (Winternight Trilogy, #1) by Katherine Arden" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Bear and the Nightingale</a> is not a perfect book. The pacing is <b>slow</b>, and sometimes I found myself losing track of the narration, as if it was something liquid slipping from my fingers. There is, though, a certain quality in it that manages to invade your senses. It is a read not meant for hot days under the sun, or sweet spring afternoons with a light breeze caressing your skin. No, it's <b>a read for frosty winter nights, with a crackling fire and the wind howling, making your blood chill and your skin shiver.</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25489134.The_Bear_and_the_Nightingale__Winternight_Trilogy___1_" title="The Bear and the Nightingale (Winternight Trilogy, #1) by Katherine Arden" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Bear and the Nightingale</a> is a vial containing the fresh scent of pines and warm honey-bread, burning incense and the crispy feel of winter winds. It's a portrait of a landscape covered in snowflakes, bordering on evil woods and the domain of the Winter King who steals maidens he showers with a prince's ransom, if he doesn't freeze them to death. It is <b>an atmospheric, haunting tale drawing on Slavic folklore</b> and myths, touching the subject of witchcraft and the inevitable clash between the gods of old times and christian doctrines and in the center of them all is a girl who does not wish to follow the path society has predetermined for her: marry or join a convent.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>❝Wild birds die in cages.❞</i>
</blockquote><br />What I admired the most about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13922215.Katherine_Arden" title="Katherine Arden" rel="nofollow noopener"> Katherine Arden</a>'s writing was the chilling ambience she created and the portayal of the <i>chyerti</i>, the little spirits or demons that are tied to households, animals, nature. There was something <b>genuine and nostalgic</b> in the way she described them, in the blurry lines between <b>sin and redemption</b>, and the answer to what is right and what is wrong lies somewhere in the middle. The same thing applies to her characters. As Vasya grows up, she is surrounded by many people, the storytelling nursemaid, the half-mad, pious step-mother, the angelic priest that preaches perdition, the family that loves but does not quite understand her. All of them play an important role in shaping Vasya's personality, with their obsessions, their tenderness and their cruelty. The wilderness in her was endearing, especially given that her intentions were pure and she kept saving everyone only to be branded as a heretic and a demon.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>❝We who live forever can know no courage, nor do we love enough to give our lives.❞</i>
</blockquote><br /><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25489134.The_Bear_and_the_Nightingale__Winternight_Trilogy___1_" title="The Bear and the Nightingale (Winternight Trilogy, #1) by Katherine Arden" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Bear and the Nightingale</a> is a story that plays its mournful tune and tugs at your soul with light touches, but affects you nonetheless.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2353814010479561998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2355167526" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2355167526" />
    <a title="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24156068-christina---recipe-a-read"><img alt="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580849831p2/24156068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2355167526?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" href="/user/show/24156068-christina---recipe-a-read">Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2355167526" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2860353980666958068"><b>5, just take them all Arden stars!!!</b><br/><br/><i>Full review along with a recipe for Zharkoye (traditional Russian beef stew) featured on my blog <a href='https://recipeandaread.wordpress.com/2019/02/06/review-recipe-the-bear-and-the-nightingale-by-katherine-arden-zharkoye-aka-russian-beef-stew/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Recipe & a Read</a>!</i><br/><br/>So, first things first in this review: I LOVED THIS BOOK. It was magical and whimsical and absolutely not what I was expecting at all. I’ve seen all the hype around this book / series, I’ve seen the fantastic reviews but for some reason I just kept glazing it over for other books. This, was a huge mistake and I wish I would’ve read it sooner because</span>
  <span id="freeText2860353980666958068" style="display:none"><b>5, just take them all Arden stars!!!</b><br /><br /><i>Full review along with a recipe for Zharkoye (traditional Russian beef stew) featured on my blog <a href="https://recipeandaread.wordpress.com/2019/02/06/review-recipe-the-bear-and-the-nightingale-by-katherine-arden-zharkoye-aka-russian-beef-stew/" rel="nofollow noopener">Recipe &amp; a Read</a>!</i><br /><br />So, first things first in this review: I LOVED THIS BOOK. It was magical and whimsical and absolutely not what I was expecting at all. I’ve seen all the hype around this book / series, I’ve seen the fantastic reviews but for some reason I just kept glazing it over for other books. This, was a huge mistake and I wish I would’ve read it sooner because this was absolutely lovely.<br /><br />So, what is up with this book? The where: medieval Russia (Rus’). The who: a daughter named Vasalisa (or Vasya) is the youngest child born to Pyotr Vladimirovich and his beautiful wife Marina. Marina dies during childbirth and is the daughter of the Grand Prince of Moscow. Not only is she royalty, but her mother was a mysterious, aloof but stunning beggar girl with rumored mystical powers. Marina never felt like she’d had her mother’s daughter and despite the risks involved, had Vasya – knowing she was destined to be of her own mothers lineage.<br /><br /><b>Now hear me. Before the end, you will pluck snowdrops at midwinter, die by your own choosing and weep for a nightingale. </b><br /><br />As Vasya grows up in the wilderness of northern Russia, she plays and learns from not just her brothers and sisters but from the folk of old. There’s the domovoi who guards her home, she finds friendship with the rusalka and a dangerous water spirit who lures people into her depths. Dunya is Vasya’s beloved nurse, and the only mother she’s ever known. Dunya is also the weaver of tales and recounts the old Russian folktale of Morozko – the frost king. As Vasya grows, she is willful, rebellious and challenges her families and communities beliefs of what a “proper” girl is to do and say. When her father remarries he brings home a young but fragile girl who is able to see the folk of the land, but considers them demons endangering her immortal soul.<br /><br />Along with Pytor and his new wife Anna comes a new priest for the townspeople, Father Konstantin, who is as handsome as he is supposed to be pious. However, beneath his golden exterior lurks something far more sinister. As Konstantin and Anna urge the townspeople to shun the spirits of old, bad and sinister things begin breaking free of their prisons from within the forest and Vasya is thrust into a magical race to see who comes out on top. Little does Vasya know, that Morozko has been doing everything in his power since she was a child to ensure their paths cross…<br /><br /><b>I would walk into the jaws of hell itself, if it were a path of my own choosing. I would rather die tomorrow in the forest than live a hundred years of the life appointed to me. </b><br /><br />This is one of the hardest books I’ve ever tried to write a concise summary for. There is so much detail, history and folklore going on, on every single page that it’s an absolutely magical whirlwind of information. When I saw all the hype surrounding this book I added it to my TBR but kept pushing it off in favor of other books that seemed to appeal to me more directly. I borrowed this book from the library and only got around to it when they told me I only had a week left until it had to be returned. It took only a few chapters for me to become completely engrossed with Vasya’s story and completely and utterly enamored with Vasya herself.<br /><br /><b>Wild birds die in cages. </b><br /><br />The Bear and the Nightingale is one of the most singularly outstanding books that I’ve read in a long time. The marriage of stunningly vivid and beautiful prose with a compelling story about a resilient girl left me aching for more. The imagery that Adren poured into this story absolutely transports the reader to an incredibly beautiful and foreign place. While I do think this book could be read any time of the year, there is something particularly magical about reading it during the winter because this definitely has all the *frosty* vibes (eh…eh….GET IT). This might be the most atmospheric novel I’ve ever read and beyond the lovely, lyrical prose and beautiful setting is this message that girls can be anything they want to be – no matter what society may dictate to them.<br /><br /><b>I do not understand “damned”. You are. And because you are, you can walk where you will, into peace, oblivion, or pits of fire, but you will always choose. </b><br /><br />This isn’t a “race to the finish” novel, it’s like watching a flower slowly bloom. The longer you wait, the more you watch, the more beautiful it becomes. Arden honored these folktales and wove an intricate and inspiring story with a resilient and inspiring main character in Vasya and I think any reader could easily find pieces of themselves within her story. This was an absolutely stunning read from the first page to the last and while it’s a bit slower than typical fantasy novels – readers of all genres would do well to pick it up!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2860353980666958068" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1798098581" />
    <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters"><img alt="Elyse  Walters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514246949p2/597461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1798098581?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781785031045" href="/book/show/25493853-the-bear-and-the-nightingale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/597461-elyse-walters?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1798098581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7809926158966265379">Wow.....*Stunning*!!!!<br/>Katherine Arden's lush and lovely debut novel deftly transports us to Russia in the 14th century with incredible lyricism- scents-sounds-vivid beauty-subtle intrigue- and gorgeous Russian folklore. <br/><br/>At the start Marina is frail and weak. She has 4 children and is pregnant with her 5th. Pyotr, her husband, and Dunya, her devoted nurse, both beg Marina not to keep the baby. They are fearful she will die. Marina had given Pyotr 3 sons and 1 daughter....but she was still hoping-</span>
  <span id="freeText7809926158966265379" style="display:none">Wow.....*Stunning*!!!!<br />Katherine Arden's lush and lovely debut novel deftly transports us to Russia in the 14th century with incredible lyricism- scents-sounds-vivid beauty-subtle intrigue- and gorgeous Russian folklore. <br /><br />At the start Marina is frail and weak. She has 4 children and is pregnant with her 5th. Pyotr, her husband, and Dunya, her devoted nurse, both beg Marina not to keep the baby. They are fearful she will die. Marina had given Pyotr 3 sons and 1 daughter....but she was still hoping- waiting - determined to give birth to a daughter that carried her mother's magical spirits - a strength that her daughter Olga wasn't born with. Marina said it would be worth leaving her children motherless, to give birth to a daughter with her mothers spirits. If she died she made Pyotr and Dunya to promise to take care of her. <br />Marina did die. Her daughter, Vasya was born with her grandmothers magical powers, and strengths. <br /><br />We soon notice Vasya has an insurmountable, unyielding amount of breezy - spunky - independent- energy. She marches the beat of a different drummer ....and she is simply irresistible. <br />The first time she got lost in the forest - ( she ran off to eat her honeycake), she was scared, cold, and shivering. She was lost in the dusk on the cusp of winter and it was going to snow. She meets a man with one gray eye and the other was missing. <br />She talks to the man. It's been a long time since he has seen a Russian girl. Vasya didn't understand what he meant- but she said:<br />"Do you know where we are?" <br />"I am lost. My father is Pyotr Vladimirovich. If you can take me home, he will see you fed, and give you a place beside the oven. It is going to snow". <br />He said he would help her -- but he wanted her to "come here" first and help him. <br />Vasya had no particular reason to be untrusting. <br />Well.....the man did frighten her. AND THIS IS WHEN I TRUELY FELL IN LOVE WITH THIS HEROINE ...because we watch her courage go in and out. One minute she speaks out strong defending herself - but then the next minute she loses faith and feels vulnerable. It's as if Vasya is AS BIG AS SHE IS SMALL... <br />and as SMALL AS SHE IS BIG. She is real - whole - so very human! <br />Her brother, Sasha finds her. She sobs..... They return home. Dunya and and her father are angry. They are worried that they Vasya is a wild child who will run off when she feels like it --and become completely unmanageable. The girl needs a mother Pyotr thinks. I'm thinking... hm? That easy huh? To control a free spirt? I was wondering how many mother's he consulted for such wisdom of his. Haha!<br /><br />Pyotr may have been angry at Vasya - wanting to punish her. BUT I WAS ANGRY AT HIM!!! <br /> "Pyotr thrashed his daughter the next day, and she wept, so he was not cruel"<br />Huh??? BEATING IS ALWAYS CRUEL......( no matter what century it is)<br />"Vasya was forbidden to leave the village, but for once, that was no hardship. She had taken chill, and she had nightmares in which she revisited a one-eye man, a horse, and a stranger in a clearing in the woods". <br /><br />My emotions were soooo invested as this story keeps changing and spinning off in surprising directions. <br />Vasya 'does' wanders back into the woods as a teenager. Around this same time evil is entering the village. Through Pyotr's marriage and a Priest....( both people to be suspicious of), demons are becoming fierce. -- but this is a fairytale ... and Vasya is the GOOD SPIRIT!!!!<br /><br />This book feels like an instant classic -- An enchanting mystical exotic world!!!!<br /><br />Thank You Random House Publishing Company, Random House, and Katherine Arden<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7809926158966265379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2328556588" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2328556588" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2328556588?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=faery-tales">faery-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=unpopular-opinions">unpopular-opinions</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2328556588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9272706234910540212"><b>My friends:</b> <i>THIS WAS JUST LIKE UPROOTED!</i><br/><b>Me:</b> <i>LIARRR!!!</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551379235ra/27132038.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Oof</i>. Good thing my friend lent me her copy because if I had <b>spent my money</b> on this – when I could have used those funds to purchase a book I <i>actually enjoyed</i> – I <b>might’ve cried</b>. <i>YIKES!</i><br/><br/>I absolutely <b>love Russian folklore</b> and literature, so I was really looking forward to this!!! You can’t even imagine the <b>disappointment</b> I’m feeling right now. <i>WHY?! WHY COULDN’T I HAVE LIKED THIS LIKE EVERYONE ELSE?!!!</i> This was just so <b>mediocre</b> and … well, <b>boring</b></span>
  <span id="freeText9272706234910540212" style="display:none"><b>My friends:</b> <i>THIS WAS JUST LIKE UPROOTED!</i><br><b>Me:</b> <i>LIARRR!!!</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551379235ra/27132038.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Oof</i>. Good thing my friend lent me her copy because if I had <b>spent my money</b> on this – when I could have used those funds to purchase a book I <i>actually enjoyed</i> – I <b>might’ve cried</b>. <i>YIKES!</i><br><br>I absolutely <b>love Russian folklore</b> and literature, so I was really looking forward to this!!! You can’t even imagine the <b>disappointment</b> I’m feeling right now. <i>WHY?! WHY COULDN’T I HAVE LIKED THIS LIKE EVERYONE ELSE?!!!</i> This was just so <b>mediocre</b> and … well, <b>boring</b>. I was nearly bored to tears. I mean, for goodness sake, it took me about <i>A MONTH</i> to slug through this. This book has been one of my most <b>miserable</b> reading experiences…<i>EVER</i> and I’ve read over 1800 books in my 23 years. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551379208ra/27132037.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Going into this, I had initially thought that this trilogy was going to be a Russia-inspired fantasy – much in the vein the Leigh Bardguo’s <i>Grisha</i> trilogy, but this is actually <b>Russian historical fiction</b>. In my experience, historical fiction has been pretty <b>hit or miss</b> for me. And in case you couldn’t tell…this was a <i>MISS</i>.<br><br>My <b>favourite aspect</b> of this novel was the <b>folklore</b>. This is what I was looking forward to the most and Katherine Arden did not disappoint in this regard. There were <b>household spirits</b> floating around. The people in the village worshipped various <b>pagan gods</b>…at least until Vasya’s new stepmother got there. And Vasya met <b>nature faeries</b> in her numerous adventures, traipsing around the woods. I definitely enjoyed the <i>rusalka</i> the most, who, in exchange for friendship and flowers, agreed to refrain from drowning men in the village. How kind of them, haha. <br><br>I also enjoyed the <b>familial dynamics</b> in the story. Vasya was such a <i>wild and carefree</i> protagonist, who hated to be tied down into the traditionally feminine roles that were expected of her. However, she wasn’t necessarily smart about it either, as she’d venture into the <b>woods</b>, which were filled with dangerous creatures, and she was oftentimes improperly dressed for such severe weather conditions. After all, this story takes place in the dead of winter…in <i>RUSSIA</i>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551374801ra/27131601.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551374801ra/27131600.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was extremely saddened when her brother Sasha left home to become a monk, leaving Vasya behind. I <i>LOVED</i> their <i>elder brother / baby sister</i> dynamic. It was such a <b>sweet relationship</b>. I was also amused over how frustrated Olga, her elder sister, got when Vasya refused to act like a proper and respectable lady, by choosing to spend her days in the woods, like some <i>wild sprite</i>.<br><br><i>Now onto what I <b>didn’t like</b>…</i><br><br>Vasya’s evil stepmother, who wanted to become a nun before her marriage to Vasya’s father was arranged, and the village’s fear-mongering priest were responsible for much of the <b>religious persecution</b> in this novel. Arden tried to tackle <b>too much</b> here because the <b>stepmother</b>, a <b>wicked pagan god</b> – who was defeated <i>WAY TOO EASILY</i>, in my opinion, and the <b>Christian religion</b> itself were <i>ALL</i> substantial antagonists in this tale. The stepmother and the priest tried to get rid of the pagan gods by pushing Christianity onto the Russian village, instead of <i>letting them choose</i> their own beliefs. And because Vasya was an unconventional young woman for the time period, she was <i>naturally</i> accused of <b>witchcraft</b>, leading to a village-wide witch hunt…which always worked in the past, of course. People accused of witchcraft were always guilty of this crime…<i>NOT</i>! <br><br>I also did not enjoy reading about the <b>marital rape</b> that occurs multiple times throughout the novel. It drew me out of the story and made me quite uncomfortable, especially since the victim <b>cries</b> while it occurs for weeks, and eventually, this even results in a pregnancy. This was a completely awful situation that I do not feel <i>HAD</i> to be included, so this definitely contributed to my distaste of the novel. Historical fiction has become <b>so progressive</b> today that it was alarming to read, even if the author was trying to stay true to the time period. If stories about 12th century England can include African characters, despite them not arriving until the 16th century, we can have stories about 14th century Russia without <b>sexual abuse</b>. <br><br>In addition, the aforementioned <i>30-year old</i> priest has extreme <b>paedophilic tendencies</b> when he lusts after <i>15-year old</i> Vasya. And then, he blames Vasya for <i>HIS</i> perverted thoughts! That was absolutely disgusting. I do not know if Arden specifically included this to call out Vatican for its recent sexual abuse scandals that’ve made headlines, <i>BUT</i> it was disgusting to read about. Seriously, <i>ICK</i>!<br><br>Despite all of my complaints thus far, the <b>main reason</b> that I disliked this novel was because <b>three-quarters</b> of the novel is <b>exposition</b>. I learnt so many <i>unnecessary details</i> about Vasya’s childhood and her stepmother’s background that did nothing to enhance my reading experience. In fact, most of the <b>plot</b> only takes place in the <b>last quarter</b> of the novel. And by the time that I got there…I just <b>didn’t care</b> anymore. I’m sorry, but I just didn’t. <br><br>I ended this book having enjoyed reading about <b>a carefree girl, a mysterious frost demon, and a talking horse</b>, but not much else. Needless to say, this was a <b>torturous reading experience</b> and I’m <b>incredibly disappointed</b>. I’ve been promised that the second and third books in the trilogy are improvements upon the first though, so I hope that I’ll be able to give the rest of this trilogy higher ratings. But if I’m being honest…I’m <i>not</i> feeling all that <b>optimistic</b> about it. <i>Sigh…</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9272706234910540212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2140614236" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2140614236" />
    <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea"><img alt="Amalia Gkavea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559158764p2/56789747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2140614236?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amalia Gkavea" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea">Amalia Gkavea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28862387-the-bear-and-the-nightingale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=american-literature">american-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=historical-fantasy">historical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=myths-legends">myths-legends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=russia">russia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2140614236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1773217528030185524"><i>
  <b>‘’Fairy tales are sweet on winter nights, nothing more.’’</b>
</i><br/><br/>Russian fairy tales are unlike any others, in my opinion.They are not simple, ‘’happily-ever-after’’ myths, but wonderfully detailed glimpses in the daily lives of people born in times gone-by and tales that hide themes that are relevant to our era. They contain female heroines that surpass inexplicable odds and many have ambiguous closures. There is a sadness that permeates the Russian fairy tale tradition and a fierceness, a strangel</span>
  <span id="freeText1773217528030185524" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>‘’Fairy tales are sweet on winter nights, nothing more.’’</b>
</i><br /><br />Russian fairy tales are unlike any others, in my opinion.They are not simple, ‘’happily-ever-after’’ myths, but wonderfully detailed glimpses in the daily lives of people born in times gone-by and tales that hide themes that are relevant to our era. They contain female heroines that surpass inexplicable odds and many have ambiguous closures. There is a sadness that permeates the Russian fairy tale tradition and a fierceness, a strangely modern idea of feminism. All these features are included in Katherine Arden’s beautiful first installment of the Winternight Trilogy.<br /><br />This book has been sitting in my TBR for practically forever, and when the second part came to me as an ARC, I thought it was finally time to begin my journey to Lesnaya Zemlya. In a Russian village, during the late medieval times, a child is born but the mother dies. Vasya has inherited the extraordinary, otherworldly gift of her mother, along with her kind heart, her free spirit of adventure and tolerance. Vasya can see what noone else is worthy to see, but her gift puts her in danger when her father decides to wed another woman. Her name is Anna, a fundamentalist as any has ever seen in any genre in Literature, and another woman who has the ability to see ‘’demons’’. Terrified of the traces of the pagan culture in her husband’s territory, she calls for a priest to come and cast away the demons. Konstantin arrives and everything in Vasya’s life changes.<br /><br />The essence of the tale is the battle between the pagan tradition and Christianity. Still, ‘’’battle’’ isn’t the right word, since this division is completely constructed by a small number of people who wish to serve their own false convictions. Before Anna came to the community, the people had found the perfect balance between the teachings of Christ and the old Russian deities and traditions. Until priests started talking of demons, fire, and eternal damnation. It’s always been a point of great discourse (and discord) in Literature and in History. In any case, Vasya, Dunya and most of the women are respectful followers of both religions. Anna cannot understand it, locked as she is in her own hallucinations and she descends into a darkness where fear and demons reign. The problem is that she takes everyone else with her.<br /><br />Arden has composed a tale out of many familiar characteristics of Russian fairy tales. The well-known legend of Lord Winter and the beautiful Maiden lies at the heart of it, while we meet the Baba Yaga, the domovoi (the peaceful spirits that protect the hearth of the Russian household), the vazila, the enchanting Rusalka...The supernatural characters become the heart of the story, because the human characters, well...they’re not very interesting. Anna would make a fine couple with the Devil she so hates (although I’d pity the poor man…), Vasya’s father is a doormat and Dunya is kind and comforting, but not that original. The one who had my unwavering attention was Konstantin, the young priest. An ambiguous character, fully conflicted, dark and perplexing as he is perplexed. He desperately wants to believe and serve but in what? In whom? His interactions with Vasilisa were brilliant and very intriguing. Besides Vasya and Konstantin, there is another major haunting character, but you’ll have to read it to discover it….<br /><br />So, does the novel worth the hype? In my opinion, yes. Absolutely and definitely. The atmosphere and the transition of the traditional story are exceptionally constructed. Do I think it would be even better if it was written by a Russian writer? Allow me to say that yes, I believe it would. You see, there is a distinctive, haunting veil of sadness, threat and death in the Russian tradition and, while these elements are present in Arden’s work, they weren’t as tense and concise as I’d like them to be. At times, the writing became a bit too YA, a genre that I do not appreciate much. This is strictly my personal opinion, formed out of many years of familiarity with Russian Literature and Culture. However, I definitely enjoyed ‘’The Bear and the Nightingale’’ and I hope that ‘’The Girl In The Tower’’ will be equally satisfying.<br /><br />My reviews can also be found on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://theopinionatedreaderblog.wordpress.com/">https://theopinionatedreaderblog.word...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1773217528030185524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2140614236">
  <td colspan="2">

  <span id="freeText18130611507905431431" style="display:none"><b>12/30/17 - TODAY ONLY! ON SALE for $2.99:</b><br><br><a href="https://www.amazon.com/Bear-Nightingale-Novel-Winternight-Trilogy-ebook/dp/B00X2FDZKW/ref=as_li_ss_il?s=digital-text&amp;ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1514664248&amp;sr=1-6&amp;linkCode=li1&amp;tag=rabrea-20&amp;linkId=5c5beee1d9e3a2d52e1841aaa6da6240" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514664291i/24801137.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514664291i/24801138.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/2EiufLU">http://amzn.to/2EiufLU</a><br><br><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2017/01/review-the-bear-and-the-nightingale-by-katherine-arden-jessicadhaluska-arden_katherine-delreybooks.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br>I added another new bookshelf to Goodreads: religious nutters<br><br>I preface my review with that statement, b/c it's important that you know exactly how off-putting I find anyone who uses religion as a crutch to excuse their abominable behavior. <br><br>Agamemnon sacrificing his daughter to ensure favorable winds as he sails to Troy? Kill him on his own alter. Spanish Inquisitioners torturing anyone not Catholic for the glory of God? Burn them at the stake. The KKK claiming that a darker skin tone is the mark of Cain to justify their prejudice and hate? String them up in their own front yard. #noimnotkidding<br><br>And I have to tell you, if it wasn't for that insufferable jackass Konstantin and the witch-hunting frenzy he worked his congregation into, THE BEAR AND THE NIGHTINGALE would have easily been a 4+ star read.<br><br>I loved Vasya and (most of) her family. I was nearly as heartbroken as her father when Sasha left to become a monk. I felt Olga's frustration and amusement at her younger sister who refused to be tamed. And when that creep Karil made eyes at Vasya, I clenched my fists and ground my teeth along with Alyosha.<br><br>More than the characters, I loved the folklore. The house spirits, the nature fae, the pagan gods . . . Vasya's world was steeped in fantastical creatures. The vodianoy who stole Kolya's basket of freshly caught fish, the rusalka who agreed to stop drowning men from the village in exchange for friendship and fresh blossoms, and the vazila who taught Vasya to speak to horses are a mere fraction of what Arden's Rus' has to offer. <br><br>And if the villains in this tale had been limited to an evil stepmother and a dark god, it would've been my perfect read. <br><br>BUT. Religion. Christianity, to be specific, hellbent on choking the life out of everything not equally Christian, and how is this best accomplished? Fear and intimidation, naturally. Also blame. It's important to have an unconventional woman at hand, the better to accuse of witchcraft when the opportunity inevitably presents itself. *flares nostrils*<br><br>I'm not trying to discredit this tactic as a viable plot device, I'm just explaining my hatred of it. It's 100% a personal preference, which is why I have zero qualms about recommending THE BEAR AND THE NIGHTINGALE to anyone who interested in reading this type of folklore-influenced fantasy. YES, even those rare individuals who hate religious nutters as much as I do--apparently, this is the first book in a trilogy, and as I'm relatively confident that said issue is resolved, which means the next book has even greater potential for awesome. <br><br>Looking forward to it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1952187231" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1952187231" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1952187231?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780399567186" href="/book/show/35738638-the-bear-and-the-nightingale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=coronavirus-read">coronavirus-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=magic-stuff">magic-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=witchy-woman">witchy-woman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=poopin-in-the-woods">poopin-in-the-woods</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fairytale">fairytale</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1952187231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer187151375424622298">This is lovely...but not much happens.<br/>I kept hearing how this was so amazing and whatnot, but it was (looking back on it) slightly boring and could have been seriously condensed. By a lot of pages.<br/><b>BUT.</b> <--that's just me.<br/>I don't dig lyrical shit all that much.<br/>Anyway, this was set in Russia, which got my attention right away. Very cool.<br/>So the (super-condensed) gist is that this girl, Vasya, is a bit magical and she does some helpful magical stuff to save all the ungrateful peasants. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514284703ra/24761882.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Only it takes</span>
  <span id="freeText187151375424622298" style="display:none">This is lovely...but not much happens.<br>I kept hearing how this was so amazing and whatnot, but it was (looking back on it) slightly boring and could have been seriously condensed. By a lot of pages.<br><b>BUT.</b> &lt;--that's just me.<br>I don't dig lyrical shit all that much.<br>Anyway, this was set in Russia, which got my attention right away. Very cool.<br>So the (super-condensed) gist is that this girl, Vasya, is a bit magical and she does some helpful magical stuff to save all the ungrateful peasants. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514284703ra/24761882.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Only it takes a long time to get to that part. <br>In fact, it takes a long time to get to <i>anything</i> remotely action-y in this book. But, unbelievably, I'm still interested. There's something here that's just undefinably good, even though I'm not one for a lot of nonsense and meandering in my books. This one definitely rambles around the point and makes you sit still while it tells you <i>everything</i> about this girl's life. I say <i>girl</i>, but she becomes a young woman while you read. And you feel like you've earned her womanhood right alongside her by the time she gets around to having her first period.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1586647992ra/29276983.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I kid, I <i>kid</i>!<br>But you honestly follow this chick from pre-birth, to birth, to childhood, to tweenhood, then into the early teens. &lt;--because this is old-timey Russia and you're a woman at 12, so Vasya is fucking old as hell by the time she sets off to confront the one-eyed old man in the woods.<br>However, you <i>do</i> really feel like you get to know these characters (all of them) inside and out. &lt;--that was nice.<br>And while I normally don't dig that slow style of storytelling, it worked better for me here than it has in other books.<br>In a good way, it kind of reminded me of the dense fairytales in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted" title="Uprooted by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36896898.Spinning_Silver" title="Spinning Silver by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Spinning Silver</a>, but I didn't <i>quite</i> enjoy this as much as either of those. Possibly because this is a trilogy and it's going to take longer to tell the complete story? Or possibly because I don't know much about Russian folklore?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587501935ra/29333711.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don't know. <br>I think I might really have given this 4 stars except for the fact that <i>weeks</i> later I'm still debating on whether or not I want to read the second book. Just the idea of jumping into something this thick and crunchy again is filling me with a sense of waffle-y-ness about the entire endeavor.<br>I'm not sure what to do. <br>Did anyone else have this problem?</span>
  <a data-text-id="187151375424622298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
